  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d277e132-cbe5-49f4-bd76-6d0908cc47c1'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14588345468101101849">A beautiful and distinguished family.<br/>A private island.<br/>A brilliant, damaged girl; a passionate, political boy.<br/>A group of four friends—the Liars—whose friendship turns destructive.<br/>A revolution. An accident. A secret.<br/>Lies upon lies.<br/>True love.<br/>The truth.<br/> <br/><i>We Were Liars</i> is a modern, sophisticated suspense novel from <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author, National Book Award finalist,</span>
  <span id="freeText14588345468101101849" style="display:none">A beautiful and distinguished family.<br />A private island.<br />A brilliant, damaged girl; a passionate, political boy.<br />A group of four friends—the Liars—whose friendship turns destructive.<br />A revolution. An accident. A secret.<br />Lies upon lies.<br />True love.<br />The truth.<br /> <br /><i>We Were Liars</i> is a modern, sophisticated suspense novel from <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author, National Book Award finalist, and Printz Award honoree E. Lockhart. <br /><br />Read it.<br /><br />And if anyone asks you how it ends, just LIE.</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/239517-why-are-they-called-the-liars-is-it-just">Why are they called the Liars? Is it just Cadence that refers to them that way? I thought they were known to the whole family as &quot;the liars&quot; and kept waiting for it to be explained...did I miss something?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_239517'><a id="like_count_community_question_239517" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/239517?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">64 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F16143347-we-were-liars">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/27535220-k"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/27535220-k">K</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Actually, the truth is that there was supposed to be a section where it explained why they were called liars due to a few scenes occurring in this spe<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Actually, the truth is that there was supposed to be a section where it explained why they were called liars due to a few scenes occurring in this specific section of the book that never made it be published. <br /><br />My sister and I had personally asked Lockhart in person at a festival a few months back and this is what she told us. There was a section that was taken off and never got to be published because it was "boring" and "slow". The publishers didn't want to slow down the book so they just cut it out. Result? A title that doesn't make sense and no longer portrays to the story the way the author intended. <br />It has *nothing* to do with the older women, the grandfather, or the Littles. It had to do with the 'Liars' (Gat, Johnny, Mirren, Cadence) and just never printed. Cady refers to her group as such, but Lockhart didn't explain any further since it was during a signing.<br /><br />edit after newer version's release: SPOILER!<br /><br />SPOILER<br />SPOILER<br />SPOILER<br /><br />*<br />*<br />*<br />*<br />SPOILER<br />SPOILER<br />SPOILER<br /><br />*<br />*<br />*<br />*<br />SPOILER<br />SPOILER<br />SPOILER<br /><br />*<br />*<br />*<br />*<br /><br />The kids were used by their mothers in an attempt in securing an inheritance. <br />Book analyzing can also include the lie of a perfect and normal life the Sinclairs lived. That beauty was a lie and Gat tried to call attention to it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I thought the same thing about them being part of her sub-conscious, until I re-read this on page 65:<br />Cady: "Seriously, Taft. You were a mess on the ph<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I thought the same thing about them being part of her sub-conscious, until I re-read this on page 65:<br />Cady: "Seriously, Taft. You were a mess on the phone last night."<br />Taft: "Was not."<br />Cady: "Were too."<br />Taft: "Mirren read me a story. Then I went to sleep. No big whup."<br /><br />Points to the supernatural. <br /><br />Also, the part that Pioup mentioned where the Aunt Carrie says about Johnny,<br /> "He's up when I'm up, sometimes. Do you see him?"<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>    </div>

    <div class="reviewControls--left">
      <span class="greyText">&nbsp;|&nbsp;</span>
    </div>
      <div class="reviewControls--left">
      <a class="uitext" id="span_class_gr-hyperlink_sort_order_span_tip_493" style="cursor: pointer; " href="#" onclick="return false"><span class="gr-hyperlink">Sort order</span></a><script>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_939616023" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/939616023" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/939616023?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=slice-of-life">slice-of-life</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=why-do-i-hate-myself">why-do-i-hate-myself</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=social-issues">social-issues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=mental-illness">mental-illness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya-contemporary">ya-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=boring-main-character">boring-main-character</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer939616023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer491437485430162156"><blockquote>
  <i>Once upon a time there were three bears who lived in a wee house in the woods.<br/>Once upon a time there were three billy goats who lived near a bridge.<br/>Once upon a time there were three soldiers, tramping together down the roads after the war.<br/>Once upon a time there were three little pigs.<br/>Once upon a time there were three brothers.<br/>No, this is it. This is the variation I want.</i>
</blockquote><b>It was a better coming of age than <i>Catcher in the Rye</i>, but I also thought <i>Twilight</i> was a better coming-of-age than <i>Catcher </i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText491437485430162156" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>Once upon a time there were three bears who lived in a wee house in the woods.<br />Once upon a time there were three billy goats who lived near a bridge.<br />Once upon a time there were three soldiers, tramping together down the roads after the war.<br />Once upon a time there were three little pigs.<br />Once upon a time there were three brothers.<br />No, this is it. This is the variation I want.</i>
</blockquote><b>It was a better coming of age than <i>Catcher in the Rye</i>, but I also thought <i>Twilight</i> was a better coming-of-age than <i>Catcher in the Rye</i></b> (fuck you, Holden Caulfield). It wasn't a terrible book. I've read far worse. It's just that the writing style sometimes get on my nerves. The sentences are sometimes written fully, and oftentimes<br />it<br />just goes like<br />this out of freaking<br />nowhere. For no freaking.<br />Reason at all. If that's the kind of thing that bothers you. Then you should probably avoid this book.<br /><br /><b>This book has almost no plot. It is full of odd sentence structures and purple prose.</b> The entire book is about a poor-little-rich-girl living with a poor-little-rich-family with the kind of ending that makes you go "WHAT THE ACTUAL KIND OF M. NIGHT SHYAMALAN FUCKERY IS THIS?!"<br /><br />It's not terrible. <b>But there's almost no plot at all.</b> The "Liars" are more "Talkers," and they have almost no relevant role in the book because this book is about a pretentious girl with nothing but <b>#whitegirlproblems</b> and <b>#richpeopleproblems</b>. <b>The aforementioned "Liars" don't do anything in this book</b>, they're not witty, they're not cute, they don't give off the sense of closeness and kinship that you get from growing up with someone their entire life. Hell, they're nowhere near <i>Dead Poets Society</i> kind of interesting.<br /><br />This is a coming of age, and nothing more. It has<br />the<br />kind<br />of writing style<br />that's often choppy<br />like this. Commas<br />are sometimes used. And sometimes not. Haphazardly. With no punctuality.<br />No pun intended.<br /><br /><b>Sentences are fragmented.</b> The main character sometimes.<br />Has the tendency to use overwrought, run on metaphors. To describe herself. And her headaches. Such as a helicopter blown by the wind tossed by the torrential rain in the wilds of Alaska felt by a little Eskimo girl during the first whispers of a glacial spring with the scent of violets and hints of lavender in the fields of Grasse.<br /><br /><u>The Summary</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>My full name is Cadence Sinclair Eastman.<br />I am nearly eighteen.<br />I used to be blond, but now my hair is black.<br />I used to be strong, but now I am weak.<br />I used to be pretty, but now I look sick.<br />It is true I suffer migraines since my accident.<br />It is true I do not suffer fools.</i>
</blockquote>Poor little Cadence Sinclair is wealthy. She is loved. She is one of the Sinclairs, a good-looking "old-money Democrat" family, think the Kennedys, without the political aspirations. They have names like Liberty, Taft, and Tipper. They go to Ivy League schools. They have trust funds. They have sired a generation of children, the leader of which is Cadence. Cadence and her crew call themselves <b>"The Liars."</b> The Liars are composed of her cousins Mirren, Johnny, and the outcast "Healthcliff," Indian love interest, Gat.<br /><br />The Liars supposedly cause trouble. They don't really. They do almost nothing. Cadence herself is sick. She is prone to theatrics, and she is not-so-secretly in love with Gat. She gets headaches. She feels self-pity. She is privileged. She doesn't realize it.<br /><br /><b>This is the story of a wealthy, beautiful family.</b><blockquote>
  <i>It’s a beautiful night, and we are indeed a beautiful family.<br />I do not know what changed.</i>
</blockquote><b>This is the story about a girl's headaches.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Why did I go into the water alone at night?<br />Where were my clothes?<br />Did I really have a head injury from the swim, or did something else happen?</i>
</blockquote><b>This is a story about The Liars. And their spectacularly brilliant conversations for the entire fucking summer.</b><blockquote>
  <i>They have baby oil spread on their bodies. Two bottles of it lie on the grass. “Aren’t you afraid you’ll get burned?” I ask.<br />“I don’t believe in sunblock anymore,” says Johnny.<br />“He’s decided the scientists are corrupt and the whole sunblock industry is a moneymaking fraud,” says Mirren.<br />“Have you ever seen sun poisoning?” I ask. “The skin literally bubbles.”<br />“It’s a dumb idea,” says Mirren. “We’re just bored out of our minds, that’s all.”</i>
</blockquote><b>They're not the only ones bored out of their mind.</b><br /><br /><u>The Writing</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>I plunge down,<br />down to rocky rocky bottom, and<br />I can see the base of Beechwood Island and<br />my arms and legs feel numb but my fingers are cold. Slices<br />of seaweed go past as I fall.<br />And then I am up again, and breathing.<br />I’m okay,<br />my head is okay,<br />no one needs to cry for me or worry about me.<br />I am fine,<br />I am alive.<br />I swim to shore.</i>
</blockquote><b>I really have a problem with the writing, but this is just a matter of taste</b>. But then again, I've never been a fan of this type of prose. Needless to say, I don't like e.e. cummings. The writing is so often choppy, haphazardly punctuated. <b>The first-person narrator also has a tendency to use very, very dramatic imagery to describe situations.</b> Some situations are false.<blockquote>
  <i>Then he pulled out a handgun and shot me in the chest. I was standing on the lawn and I fell. The bullet hole opened wide and my heart rolled out of my rib cage and down into a flower bed. Blood gushed rhythmically from my open wound,<br />then from my eyes,<br />my ears,<br />my mouth.</i>
</blockquote>That, there, was a description of how she FELT. <b>It confused me as fuck until I realized that she didn't actually get hurt, which made it even more confusing when she did actually hurt herself.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Every time Gat said these things, so casual and truthful, so oblivious—my veins opened. My wrists split. I bled down my palms. I went light-headed.</i>
</blockquote><b>I thought that was her being overdramatic again</b>, until I realized that the guy was fucking bandaging her up afterwards.<br /><br />The main character has a huge tendency to use <b>purple prose.</b> She describes her migraines like they were the end of the world, which, I understand to some people they might be, but <b>if you're getting a fucking migraine, there's really no bloody need to get all freaking poetic about it.</b><blockquote>
  <i>A witch has been standing there behind me for some time, waiting for a moment of weakness. She holds an ivory statue of a goose. It is intricately carved. I turn and admire it only for a moment before she swings it with shocking force. It connects, crushing a hole in my forehead. I can feel my bone come loose. The witch swings the statue again and hits above my right ear, smashing my skull. Blow after blow she lands, until tiny flakes of bone litter the bed and mingle with chipped bits of her once-beautiful goose.</i>
</blockquote><b>That entire passage is one of many throughout the book about her headaches.</b> I just couldn't take it.<br /><br /><u>The Main Character</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>“You’re filled with superiority, aren’t you? You think you understand the world so much better than I do. I’ve heard Gat talking. I’ve seen you eating up his words like ice cream off a spoon. But you haven’t paid bills, you haven’t had a family, owned property, seen the world. You have no idea what you’re talking about, and yet you do nothing but pass judgment.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Poor-little-rich-girl</b> syndrome. She's beautiful, but wounded, and "mysterious" and revered, just for the sake of her blood alone, for the sake of her family's name alone. Think about it. If you were a Kennedy, it doesn't matter if you look like an elephant stepped on your head when you were born. People are still going to love you and worship you and whisper your name with reverence because you're a motherfucking Kennedy. It's this way with the Sinclairs, only there's no paparazzi following them around. All of the benefits, and no family curse. But somehow Cadence finds a way to be a <b>rebel-without-a-cause anyway.</b><br /><br />She's rich. She's hypocritical about her wealth because she criticizes her own fucking family for being wealthy. She does stupid shit like give things away to random people because she can. <b>Before the summer is over, Cadence's room will have been empty because she keeps giving shit away for no fucking reason.</b><br /><br /><b>Cadence is unaware of others.</b> She is spoiled. She takes her wealth for granted. <b>She doesn't pay any attention to "the help."</b><blockquote>
  <i>One night, the four of us ate a picnic down on the tiny beach. Steamed clams, potatoes, and sweet corn. The staff made it. I didn’t know their names.</i>
</blockquote><b>I'm sorry, but I can't sympathize with such a whiny person who's completely unaware of how privileged she is, headaches be damned.</b><blockquote>
  <i>“Who are Ginny and Paulo?”<br />Gat hits his fist into his palm. “Ginny is the housekeeper. Paulo is the gardener. You don’t know their names and they’ve worked here summer after summer. That’s part of my point.”<br />My face heats with shame. “I’m sorry.”</i>
</blockquote><u>The Love Interest</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>“You’re saying Granddad thinks you’re Heathcliff?”<br />“I promise you, he does,” says Gat. “A brute beneath a pleasant surface, betraying his kindness in letting me come to his sheltered island every year—I’ve betrayed him by seducing his Catherine, his Cadence. And my penance is to become the monster he always saw in me.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Gat is the only interesting character in the book.</b> He is Indian-American. Gat Patil. He is the nephew of her aunt's boyfriend, and they've known each other for years. He is self-aware. Too self-aware in the pretentious way that teenagers can often be, but his character feels authentically teenaged. I liked him. He is accepted into The Liars, but he's not altogether accepted in the family. Because of his skin color, because of his lack of family money, he feels left out. And I can sympathize with him.<blockquote>
  <i>“I’m not saying he wants to be the guy who only likes white people,” Gat went on. “He knows he’s not supposed to be that guy. He’s a Democrat, he voted for Obama—but that doesn’t mean he’s comfortable having people of color in his beautiful family.”</i>
</blockquote>Gat is intelligent. Reasonable. Likeable. And I wonder why the fuck he cares about a waste of air like Cadence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="491437485430162156" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1000270098?book_show_action=true">Jul 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1000270098" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17598041989276368081"> <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394730ra/760050.gif' width='500' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is the kind of book that, when I finish reading it, I’m like <i>FINALLY</i> and then throw the book out of the window (in this case not applicable because of digital copy so I'm doing it through a gif.) <br/><br/>But really, what a weird story and an uncomfortable and pretentious atmosphere this <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16143347.We_Were_Liars' title='We Were Liars by E. Lockhart' rel='nofollow noopener'>We Were Liars</a> book has. It wasn’t long, thank God, but damn it was painful to read. This is my 3rd negative review/read this week and I’m seriously pissed but will try to keep it cool.<br/><br/>I didn’t get<br/>the purpose of thi</span>
  <span id="freeText17598041989276368081" style="display:none"> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380394730ra/760050.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is the kind of book that, when I finish reading it, I’m like <i>FINALLY</i> and then throw the book out of the window (in this case not applicable because of digital copy so I'm doing it through a gif.) <br><br>But really, what a weird story and an uncomfortable and pretentious atmosphere this <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16143347.We_Were_Liars" title="We Were Liars by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">We Were Liars</a> book has. It wasn’t long, thank God, but damn it was painful to read. This is my 3rd negative review/read this week and I’m seriously pissed but will try to keep it cool.<br><br>I didn’t get<br>the purpose of this book.<br>Why were they called<br>Liars anyway? Okay<br>they lied but who doesn’t?<br>Why are they supposed to<br>be so <br>special? Because<br>some of them are rich? So what?<br>Many people are as well and it <br>doesn’t make them<br>more<br>interesting/special.<br><br>(Did it annoy you? How I just wrote what I wrote? If it did, this is not the book for you.)<br><br>It’s like the author wanted to make this story ‘phenomenal’ and so damn poignant and thought that by adding some metaphorical sentences, a different writing style and a heavy recycled subject she would succeed. But she didn’t. At least, not for me. I personally thought it felt very pretentious and TOO MUCH. The pacing is uneven and the story very repetitive. The characters, except maybe for Cady, the MC, are one dimensional and I couldn’t connect with any one of them.<br><br>Again with the subject, is it mainly about...rich-wants-to-date-‘poor’-guy-aka-love-of-her-life-but-can-t-because-family? So confusing... but I guess that’s it since THAT started a lot of stuff. The love story, by the way, is so so so dull. This is all because of the hype…<br><br>Oh, the hype was there. It.IS.There. But we all know hype lies and loves doing it. <br><br>This is not the type of book I usually read because it feels, just by reading the ‘synopsis’ (really? couldn’t this book have at least a normal synopsis?) too sad/dark/eerie for me but, HEY, we all need to step out of our comfort zone from time to time. PLUS, John Green praised this book. He <br><br>''<b>Thrilling, beautiful, and blisteringly smart, <i>We Were Liars</i> is utterly unforgettable.</b><br>John Green, #1 <i>New York Times</i> bestselling author of <i>The Fault in Our Stars</i>''<br><br>praised this book. And, since I finished reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11870085.The_Fault_in_Our_Stars" title="The Fault in Our Stars by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">The Fault in Our Stars</a> not so long ago and loved it, I thought I’d trust Green’s judgement. <br><br>Except, it was boring. Boring. Boring. Boring. The only parts I felt myself enjoying reading are the little ‘stories’ with the king and his 3 daughters. <br><br>I really don’t recommend this book. It’s a waste of time because it’s confusing as hell and doesn’t even have a nice/normally written ending.<br><br>I wish I could burn it.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17598041989276368081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Ariel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel"><img alt="Ariel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1530557165p2/6536286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/966826470?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ariel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ariel" href="/user/show/6536286-ariel">Ariel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385741262" href="/book/show/18339662-we-were-liars">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer966826470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17378731793751801152">This was, without a doubt, one of the most powerful and well-crafted books I have read in a really long time. <br/><br/>Elements that made this book outstanding:<br/>1) It started with a map and a family tree. Talk about setting yourself up for success!<br/>2) The personification of emotion. This might not make sense unless you've read the book, but wow it was powerful.<br/>3) The use of fairy tales from the main character to describe situations.<br/>4) The sense of complete mystery and suspicion: I was always questioning ev</span>
  <span id="freeText17378731793751801152" style="display:none">This was, without a doubt, one of the most powerful and well-crafted books I have read in a really long time. <br /><br />Elements that made this book outstanding:<br />1) It started with a map and a family tree. Talk about setting yourself up for success!<br />2) The personification of emotion. This might not make sense unless you've read the book, but wow it was powerful.<br />3) The use of fairy tales from the main character to describe situations.<br />4) The sense of complete mystery and suspicion: I was always questioning everything.<br />5) The use of dramatic lines. You know when an author brings in an epic moment-stopping line? This was full of those awesome drops!<br />6) The moment. There's a moment where all is revealed and IT WAS PERFECT.<br />7) The consequential understanding. Everything suddenly clicked into place and it was glorious.<br />8) The side characters. I think sometimes side characters can feel inconsequential and here they felt really important.<br /><br />There weren't very many things I didn't like, to be honest, but there was one:<br />1) The title. It does't make sense to me. I don't want to say anything in case spoilers, but I don't think it's the perfect title.<br /><br />Two final things:<br />1) I have a theory. I have a theory about this book that I'm really excited to discuss so I'm going to make a video about it!<br />2) This book really made me cry. Like explode cry. Lots of tears. And I've only ever cried at 2 other books.<br /><br />I absolutely recommend this book, to everyone who likes books, because MAN, THIS WAS A GOOD BOOK.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17378731793751801152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9733250164571233719">It's true what they're saying: you're better off if I tell you nothing about this book.<br/><br/>So I will just say two things.<br/><br/>1) It is worth reading. Even though I only gave it 3 stars.<br/><br/>2) I gave it 3 stars because of the writing style, which irritated the hell out of me.   <span id="freeText9733250164571233719" style="display:none">It's true what they're saying: you're better off if I tell you nothing about this book.<br /><br />So I will just say two things.<br /><br />1) It is worth reading. Even though I only gave it 3 stars.<br /><br />2) I gave it 3 stars because of the writing style, which irritated the hell out of me. The fact that it got 3 stars after annoying me so much will hopefully give you some indication of how much I liked the idea.<br /><br />It's a very clever book and an incredibly sophisticated piece of YA. BUT... an execution that was not to my tastes. The writing was too choppy and fragmented and I hated the frequent use of nouns as adjectives. Like this:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>"His nose was dramatic, his mouth sweet. Skin deep brown, hair black and waving. Body wired with energy. Gat seemed spring-loaded. Like he was searching for something. He was contemplation and enthusiasm. Ambition and strong coffee. I could have looked at him forever."</b>
</i><br /></span>

        <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys">Shelby *trains flying monkeys*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer13387111083403361528">It's been awhile since I have so totally hated a book.<br/><a href='http://imgur.com/yDXbae3' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422464775ra/13504090.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>

</a><br/>Some of them liked/loved it.<br/><a href='http://imgur.com/DQJxMFK' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422464775ra/13504092.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/>I still love them....<br/><br/>Let's get to why I hated this so very frigging much.<br/><a href='http://imgur.com/Od95vkr' rel='nofollow noopener'>

  <blockquote>Welcome to the beautiful Sinclair family.<br/>No one is a criminal.<br/>No one is an addict.<br/>No one is a failure.<br/>The Sinclairs are athletic, tall and handsome. </blockquote>
</b><br/>That's actually </span>
  <span id="freeText13387111083403361528" style="display:none">It's been awhile since I have so totally hated a book.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/yDXbae3" rel="nofollow noopener">

</b><br>That's actually the good part on her family. In some parts of the book the author tries and make the character act like she has redeeming qualifications-but then a short few pages later I just want to smash her again.<br><a href="http://imgur.com/ajtg08f" rel="nofollow noopener">

Tell him the ones from the Boston house. The cream ones with the embroidery."<br>It was easiest to tell her I would.<br>And later, I told her I had.<br>But Bess has asked Mirren to do the same thing,<br>and neither one of us<br>begged Granddad<br>for the fucking tablecloths.</blockquote></b><br><br>Then that lovely twist of an ending:<br>I'm probably going to hell for this but don't click if you gonna whine...<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I thought it was the burning of the house<a href="http://imgur.com/810bCk7" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1422464775ra/13504095.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br>but noooooo...it's that they are all fucking dead..except for princess dumbass. <div id="review_758586688" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/758586688" />
    <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair"><img alt="Steph Sinclair" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457555690p2/4642710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/758586688?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Sinclair" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Sinclair" href="/user/show/4642710-steph-sinclair">Steph Sinclair</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780804168403" href="/book/show/18340003-we-were-liars">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People who like mind fucks</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Steph by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=2014-release">2014-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=mind-blowing-good">mind-blowing-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=yabc">yabc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=surprised-me">surprised-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=interesting-little-creature">interesting-little-creature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=random-house">random-house</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4642710-steph-sinclair?shelf=omg-that-ending">omg-that-ending</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer758586688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15149776965532850992">I went into <em>We Were Liars</em> one cocky son of a biscuit eater, feeling above it all right from page one. I'd seen this book talked about so heavily by other bloggers and how some never saw the twist coming or how others <em>totally</em> saw that twist coming. All the while, I was sitting on the sidelines with my shades on, posted up with my arms folded, saying, "Yeah, yeah, yeah. Hot potato." That's not to say I didn't <em>want</em> to read this book, because I did. I even had an ARC sitting on my shelf for the long</span>
  <span id="freeText15149776965532850992" style="display:none">I went into <em>We Were Liars</em> one cocky son of a biscuit eater, feeling above it all right from page one. I'd seen this book talked about so heavily by other bloggers and how some never saw the twist coming or how others <em>totally</em> saw that twist coming. All the while, I was sitting on the sidelines with my shades on, posted up with my arms folded, saying, "Yeah, yeah, yeah. Hot potato." That's not to say I didn't <em>want</em> to read this book, because I did. I even had an ARC sitting on my shelf for the longest time, but due to a lot of the hype, I kept putting it off. Plus, I'm one of those people who usually can easily figure out a plot twist and I didn't want to dive into something where a lot of people already mentioned figuring it out.<br><br>But one thing did nag me a little in the back of my mind was that my Bookish Twin, Blythe from <a href="http://findingblissinbooks.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Finding Bliss in Books</a>, LOVED it. I highly value her opinion when it comes to books, because we almost always agree. So when I happened to get my hands on the audiobook, I thought, "What the hell? I was supposed to read and review this anyway, right?" Let me tell you... WHOA.<br><br><strong>***First off, I just wanna say that I don't know how the print compares to the audio and that it's possible I loved the book more than others because of the  excellent job of the narrator. I can see how the fragmented sentences could be a pain to read, but this might be one of those cases where it <em>sounds</em> better out loud. That being said, I if you haven't read this book, possibly check out the audio version first.***</strong><br><br>Anyway, I was feeling very blasé about the first half. It felt like a really random story about a rich, white girl and her white girl problems, crying her white girl tears and I felt myself unsure about what the point of it all was.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404786292i/10283290._SY540_.jpg" alt="blase" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And maybe that makes me sound extremely heartless, but I couldn't relate to the main character (no, I'm not even going to tell you her name because I want you to go in blind). But somewhere along the lines, I started to become intrigued with the story because <strong>it became this strange, wild thing that I couldn't piece together</strong>.<br><br>Lockhart uses a very odd narration with fragmented sentences and strange descriptions, but I thought it was beautiful and unique. It added a very creepy layer on top the the existing oddness. It makes you question the main character, her account of the incident and the entire book. She's not very reliable and has the habit to cut off mid-sentence. I'm not sure if that was used as a way to distract the reader or if it was to used to make us question her sanity. Maybe a little bit of both. Either way, it worked on me.<br><br>As things started to heat up and I reached the cusp of the climax, the narrator's voice increased in intensity. She began talking faster, became very emotional, then suddenly on the verge of tears!<br><br>And I started thinking to myself, OH GOD NO. WHAT IS HAPPENING.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404786292i/10283291._SY540_.jpg" alt="horror" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And then IT was revealed and I was all, "WHAT IS THIS LIFE? I REJECT EVERYTHING ABOUT THIS ENDING. NOOOOOOO!!!!"<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404786292i/10283292._SY540_.jpg" alt="Nooooooo!" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, naturally, I had a good cry and needed someone to hold me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1404786292i/10283293._SY540_.jpg" alt="crying" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>By the end, I was all:<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/Cuddlebuggery/status/476424221351247872">https://twitter.com/Cuddlebuggery/sta...</a><br><br>I know this review might not be the most helpful in the world, but it's true what everyone says about <em>We Were Liars</em>. You should absolutely go in blind, with no expectations and let this book take your feels as it sees fit. If you are a fan of psychological thrillers like Stephanie Kuehn's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16045088-charm-strange?ac=1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Charm and Strange</em>
</a> or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18404113-complicit" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <em>Complicit</em>
</a>, than this one may be up your alley. I'll be here to hold you when you're finish.<br><br>ARC was provided by the publisher via <a href="http://yabookscentral.com" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Books Central</a>.<br><br>More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebugery</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15149776965532850992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_868828257" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/868828257" />
    <a title="karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45618-karen"><img alt="karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596291582p2/45618.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/868828257?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="karen" href="/user/show/45618-karen">karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=why-yes-i-ya">why-yes-i-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/45618-karen?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer868828257" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9431883145351977376">so, just like <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6948436.Little_Bee' title='Little Bee by Chris Cleave' rel='nofollow noopener'>Little Bee</a>, this book begs you "NOOO, DON'T TELL ITS SEEEEKRITS!!" and <i>if anyone asks you how it ends, just LIE.</i><br/><br/>so part of me is tempted to write this whole long review about how this book is a magical adventure focusing on a young girl in manhattan during the blackout of 2003, when all the red pandas living in the sewers came out to play, carrying tiny flashlights and shepherding people from manhattan to their homes in the outer boroughs and all the lessons this young girl learns </span>
  <span id="freeText9431883145351977376" style="display:none">so, just like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6948436.Little_Bee" title="Little Bee by Chris Cleave" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Bee</a>, this book begs you "NOOO, DON'T TELL ITS SEEEEKRITS!!" and <i>if anyone asks you how it ends, just LIE.</i><br><br>so part of me is tempted to write this whole long review about how this book is a magical adventure focusing on a young girl in manhattan during the blackout of 2003, when all the red pandas living in the sewers came out to play, carrying tiny flashlights and shepherding people from manhattan to their homes in the outer boroughs and all the lessons this young girl learns along the way from her red panda guide about life and humanity and art history and, ultimately, herself. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1393900851ra/8780273.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>because i would read that book.<br><br>instead, i am just going to say that it is perhaps unwise to market a book in this way. true, the only reason i read it myself was because i came across it when making YA list for work, and i was all "SECRETS?? I LOVE SECRETS!! I WANT TO KNOW THE SECRETS!!" it's a very effective way of drumming up interest around a book.<br><br>but the problem is, when you are <i>prepared</i> for a big twist, it is very easy to <i>guess</i> the big twist, which i did very early on. if you think you are just reading a book about some rich family and a girl with a faulty memory and a mysterious summer, with no tantalizingly bossy instructions about keeping the book's secrets, you might be more surprised when the reveal is revealed. but when such a big deal is made of SHHHHHHH, and you know you are expecting something unexpected, you will probably find it, and so reading the book just becomes an exercise in waiting for the character to figure it out. which is fine, but less effective in terms of shock value.<br><br>i liked it anyway, but i think it would have been more fun to gasp in genuine surprise at the path it took. so forget i said anything, forget what the synopsis tells you to do, and just read it like you would any other book.<br><br>this should help you forget everything you have ever known:<br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://wac.450f.edgecastcdn.net/80450F/thefw.com/files/2013/07/Nap.gif">http://wac.450f.edgecastcdn.net/80450...</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1528725630i/25720315.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><a href="http://bloggycomelately.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">come to my blog!</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9431883145351977376" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2388430485" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2388430485" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2388430485?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471403989" href="/book/show/20935171-we-were-liars">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2388430485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6940490181241645999"><i>”We were warm and shivering,<br/>and young and ancient,<br/>and alive."</i><br/><br/>When I began to read this book I went in completely blind and had absolutely no clue what it was about. The blurb on the back didn’t tell me anything about the plot and everything I knew was that <b>“We Were Liars”</b> had apparently won the YA Goodreads Choice Award in 2014. <br/>So yeah, I just decided to read it and hoped it would be good and looking at it in retrospective this actually was the best decision I could have made! ;-P <br/><br/>Because let’s</span>
  <span id="freeText6940490181241645999" style="display:none"><i>”We were warm and shivering,<br />and young and ancient,<br />and alive."</i><br /><br />When I began to read this book I went in completely blind and had absolutely no clue what it was about. The blurb on the back didn’t tell me anything about the plot and everything I knew was that <b>“We Were Liars”</b> had apparently won the YA Goodreads Choice Award in 2014. <br />So yeah, I just decided to read it and hoped it would be good and looking at it in retrospective this actually was the best decision I could have made! ;-P <br /><br />Because let’s face it, this book will mess with your head big time. <br />The Liars will make you wonder, they’ll make you question what happened in summer 15 and you’ll not only become curious but you’ll also feel a need to read on. XD<br /><br /><i>”Silence is a protective coating over pain.”</i><br /><br />Of course there are plenty of hints, but will you be able to figure them out or will you be in the dark until the end? <br />I guess by now you already realised that this isn’t one of my typical reviews and yes, you’re right. I won’t write anything about the plot. Sorry?! No, I think I’m not. *lol*<br /><br /><i>”A brute beneath a pleasant surface, betraying his kindness in letting me come to his sheltered island every year – I’ve betrayed him by seducing his Catherine, his Cadence. And my penance is to become the monster he always saw in me.”</i> <br /><br />This is a book you’ll have to experience for yourself! And I want you all to scream: <b>”WHAT THE FREAKING HELL!!??”</b> when you finally reach the ending. Haha!<br />And before you ask, yes I screamed it loud and clear!!! XD This story is a mindfuck and even my (usually very) observant mind wasn’t ready for the finale! ;-P<br /><br />So all I’m going to do is to give you a little character description. The rest you’ll have to figure out on your own. XD<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Meet the Liars:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Mirren:</b><br /><i>”She is sugar. She is curiosity and rain.”</i><br /><i>”Be a little kinder than you have to.”</i><br /><br /><b>Johnny:</b><br /><i>”He is bounce. He is effort and snark.”</i><br /><i>”Never eat anything bigger than your ass.”</i><br /><br /><b>Gat:</b><br /><i>”Do not accept an evil you can change.”</i> <br /><i>”His nose was dramatic, his mouth sweet. Skin deep borwn, hair black and waving. Body wired with energy. Gat seemed spring-loaded. Like he was searching for something. He was contemplation and enthusiasm. Ambition and strong coffee. I could have looked at him forever.”</i><br /><br /><b>Cady:</b><br /><i>”Always do what you are afraid to do,” I say.</i> <br /><i>”These days she is a gnarled crone, touching the raw flesh of my brain with her cruel fingernails. She pokes my exposed nerves, exploring whether she’ll take up residence in my skull. If she gets in, I’m confined to my bedroom for a day or maybe two.”</i><br /><br />Are you curious and intrigued already? <br /><br />If yes, I hope you’ll enjoy the book as much as I did. It was a really nice and fast read and it definitely exceeded my expectations. <br />No! Truth be told, it completely messed with my mind. <br />But we all love deliberate confusion, don’t we? ;-P<br /><br /><i>”I suffer migraines. I do not suffer fools.<br />I like a twist of meaning.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="6940490181241645999" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2136964249" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2136964249" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2136964249?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2136964249" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer74214403801708387">Cadence and her family spend every summer on a private island, courtesy of her <b>racist and classist grandfather. </b><br/><br/>All of her aunts constantly vie for the grandfather's <b>attention and favor </b>(in an attempt to keep ahold of the family fortune).<br/><br/>Cadence and her cousins consider themselves above such petty actions and spend most summers<b> making trouble, being rich </b>and taking advantage of the liquor bar. <br/><br/>Then, two summers ago, something <b>terrible and tragic </b>happens. <br/><br/>Everyone knows but Candace... and everyon</span>
  <span id="freeText74214403801708387" style="display:none">Cadence and her family spend every summer on a private island, courtesy of her <b>racist and classist grandfather. </b><br /><br />All of her aunts constantly vie for the grandfather's <b>attention and favor </b>(in an attempt to keep ahold of the family fortune).<br /><br />Cadence and her cousins consider themselves above such petty actions and spend most summers<b> making trouble, being rich </b>and taking advantage of the liquor bar. <br /><br />Then, two summers ago, something <b>terrible and tragic </b>happens. <br /><br />Everyone knows but Candace... and everyone absolutely refuses to tell her. <br /><br />And she's bound and determined to find out, one way or another. <br /><br />I don't want to go into too much depth with the plot because I strongly feel that by giving away the twist (even hints at the twist) would <b>completely ruin the novel.</b> <br /><br />The twist was literally the only thing that kept me going. <br /><br />Candace <i>(ooo, that girl...)</i> is such a great example of why kids should be given hard limits. <br /><br />This chick literally goes to a private island every summer.... and all she does is<b><i> whine</i> </b> about it. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Constantly. </i>
</b><br /><br />I guess I understand why the author does this, by the end of the novel, I felt <b>
  <i>so</i>
</b> bad for this<b>
  <i> poor </i>
</b>little girl, who only could go to a<b>
  <i> single</i>
</b> island every summer. <br /><br />Honestly, I don't know how she could handle it. <br /><br />I suppose she did have one, overarching hobby: love. <br /><br />I'm not kidding. Her only hobby is waxing poetic about how <b> how in love she is.</b><br /><br /> And this is not normal love,<b> <u>this is YA love</u> </b><i>(shudders). </i> <br /><br />Which is a whole other class of adoration. <br /><br />There's this: <blockquote>
  <i>He was contemplation and enthusiasm. Ambition and strong coffee. I could have looked at him forever.</i>
</blockquote>and this: <blockquote>
  <i>The universe was good because he was in it.</i>
</blockquote> AND THIS! <blockquote>
  <i>I wanted to touch him like he was a bunny, a kitten, something so special and soft your fingertips can’t leave it alone.</i>
</blockquote> <b>Gag. </b>Her talking about love nearly made me put the book down. <br /><br />In typical YA fashion, she is more in<b> love with the idea of being love</b> than feeling any emotion.<br /><br />Annnd...that's all there was that wasn't directly connected with the twist. Just her whining on and on about how much she loves the boy OR about how her rich family. Fab.<br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />The reader did her best with what she was given.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="74214403801708387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_970031921" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/970031921" />
    <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister"><img alt="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486056026p2/4971692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/970031921?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister" href="/user/show/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister">Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Kristin (KC) - Traveling Sister by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=powerful">powerful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=weepy">weepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=suspenseful">suspenseful</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4971692-kristin-kc---traveling-sister?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer970031921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3575255317250796195"><b>*5 Stars*<br/><br/>There’s not even a Scrabble word for how I’m feeling right now…</b><br/><br/>This story left me defeated, but its tragedy was paired equally with an unconventional beauty. It gripped me instantly to the point where I couldn’t stop thinking about its mystery…<br/><br/>Its intrigue. <br/><br/>Its quiet calamity. <br/><br/>The suspense is painted on rather thickly, which is not to say that readers will not form an accurate theory early on. But the journey remains worth it whether you’ve Sherlock Holmes’d this one or not. <br/><br/>The plot in</span>
  <span id="freeText3575255317250796195" style="display:none"><b>*5 Stars*<br><br>There’s not even a Scrabble word for how I’m feeling right now…</b><br><br>This story left me defeated, but its tragedy was paired equally with an unconventional beauty. It gripped me instantly to the point where I couldn’t stop thinking about its mystery…<br><br>Its intrigue. <br><br>Its quiet calamity. <br><br>The suspense is painted on rather thickly, which is not to say that readers will not form an accurate theory early on. But the journey remains worth it whether you’ve Sherlock Holmes’d this one or not. <br><br>The plot introduces itself in a vague manner and slowly unravels. I found that the messages held more power than the characters delivering them—the sum was definitely greater than its parts. Which fit the tone nicely.<br><br>This review may seem just as ambiguous as the story itself, but it must be if you wish to obtain the full effect of its delivery. <br><br>I will say this, however: <i>We Were Liars</i> is a haunting portrayal of a group of teenagers who have formed a sacred bond; each one striving to be free and longing for acceptance. They consider <i>love</i> more important than social and economic stature, and are displeased with the prejudices surrounding their world. <br><br>They are young. <br>They are passionate. <br>They are imperfect. <br><br>They each suffer their own personal injustice. And this is <i>their</i> story.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>What if we could somehow stop being the Beautiful Sinclair Family and just be a family? What if we could stop being different colors , different backgrounds, and just be in love?</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>The writing was unique and although it may not suit everyone’s taste, I relished it. I thought the author’s use of descriptive imagery was creative and applied with a gentle hand—nothing over-the-top or showy. <br><br>The story is told through the voice of a confused, emotional, and dejected eighteen year old girl—and the writing remained consistent with her distinctive perspective. It was poetic and profound—drifting in as a gentle breeze and building to the swirling force of a hurricane. It may not knock your socks off, but it certainly took my breath away. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>She made me act normal. Because I was. Because I could. She told me to breathe and sit up.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I’d recommend this book to anyone who enjoys a plot that persuades you to wonder. To readers who can accept the bittersweet circumstances of life displayed within their fiction. This is not a character-driven novel. The story shines brighter. I don't think I ever fully connected with any character at all--and the fact that I was moved to tears by the finish is what made this a five-star read for me. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Someone once wrote that a novel should deliver a series of small astonishments. I get the same thing spending an hour with you.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>Although I found this story entirely unique, if I had to compare, I’d say its structure reminds me a bit of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">On the Jellicoe Road</a>. Its haunting tone, as well. <br><br>A truly addictive, out-of-the-box read!<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>The universe is seeming really huge right now,” he told me. “I need something to hold on to.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2mh7uop" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="50" width="50" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380347313i/701667.jpg" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><b>
  <u>Book Stats:</u>
</b><br><b>▪	 Genre/Category:</b> YA<br><b>▪ Romance:</b> Young but present <br><b>▪	 Characters:</b> Teens struggling to find their way<br><b>▪	 Plot:</b> Mysterious. Twists slowly unravel<br><b>▪ Writing:</b> Poetic. Simple yet profound. <br><b>▪ POV:</b> First person: Heroine<br><b>▪	 Cliffhanger:</b> None. Standalone<br><b>▪  HEA? </b><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Not a conventional HEA, no. But somewhat... <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/131922-mark-monday?shelf=teenworld">teenworld</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1110126087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16098224967029298718"><a href='http://s181.photobucket.com/user/markmonday/media/I%20hate%20thinking_zpsgx4pgezq.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433227239i/15067905.jpg' alt=' photo I hate thinking_zpsgx4pgezq.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>well this was all kinds of pointless<br/>and also depressing. <br/>ugh! <br/><br/>the writing is so mannered<br/>it is an affectation<br/>a studied display of real or pretended feeling.<br/>the whole book lacks affect;<br/>it lacks the real emotion<br/>that it so desperately tries to convey<br/>in its own affect-less way.<br/>the writer has talent<br/>sure<br/>but here it is squandered.<br/><br/>I like the premise, it's enticing;<br/>who doesn't want to read about <br/>the fragile cloistered lives <br/>of insular rich white people<br/>who summer on their own private island?<br/>makes us no</span>
  <span id="freeText16098224967029298718" style="display:none"><a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/user/markmonday/media/I%20hate%20thinking_zpsgx4pgezq.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433227239i/15067905.jpg" alt=" photo I hate thinking_zpsgx4pgezq.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>well this was all kinds of pointless<br>and also depressing. <br>ugh! <br><br>the writing is so mannered<br>it is an affectation<br>a studied display of real or pretended feeling.<br>the whole book lacks affect;<br>it lacks the real emotion<br>that it so desperately tries to convey<br>in its own affect-less way.<br>the writer has talent<br>sure<br>but here it is squandered.<br><br>I like the premise, it's enticing;<br>who doesn't want to read about <br>the fragile cloistered lives <br>of insular rich white people<br>who summer on their own private island?<br>makes us not-rich people feel better<br>reading about the miserable rich.<br>I guess?<br><br><a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/user/markmonday/media/tumblr_np6owxgOij1qz6f9yo1_540_zpsdqnaaeim.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433227701i/15067959._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo tumblr_np6owxgOij1qz6f9yo1_540_zpsdqnaaeim.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>but why go to all that trouble<br>setting up class critique<br>and racial tensions<br>and family drama<br>and dressing it up in fairy tale finery<br>when that will all just be thrown away<br>on a maudlin twist ending<br>with a corny moral message:<br>"Be a little kinder"...<br>ugh!<br><br>those ideas went nowhere<br>those ideas were rendered pointless<br>because in the end the book <br>is not a scouring brillo pad after all,<br>it's just another soppy wet sponge.<br><br>rub that sponge on your face<br>it will look like you cried!<br><br><a href="http://s181.photobucket.com/user/markmonday/media/no%20time%20for%20your%20tears_zpsv14edffs.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a></span>

<div id="review_933225060" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/933225060" />
    <a title="Candace" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16384209-candace"><img alt="Candace" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459720769p2/16384209.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/933225060?book_show_action=true">Mar 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candace" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candace" href="/user/show/16384209-candace">Candace</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=listened-to-audio-version">listened-to-audio-version</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=forbidden-romance">forbidden-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=childhood-loves">childhood-loves</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=sweet-heart-warming-stories">sweet-heart-warming-stories</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16384209-candace?shelf=shocking-twists">shocking-twists</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer933225060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9373049168297849585">I went into 'We Were Liars' blind, for the most part. It had been sitting on my Audible shelf for so long that I had long-since forgotten what it was supposed to be about. Sometimes, I get it in my head that a book is going to be about something, when it absolutely has nothing to do with it. God only knows where I get these ideas, but I do. As a result, I often find myself being surprised by the content of the stories I read without re-reading the blurbs. This was one of those times. Note to oth</span>
  <span id="freeText9373049168297849585" style="display:none">I went into 'We Were Liars' blind, for the most part. It had been sitting on my Audible shelf for so long that I had long-since forgotten what it was supposed to be about. Sometimes, I get it in my head that a book is going to be about something, when it absolutely has nothing to do with it. God only knows where I get these ideas, but I do. As a result, I often find myself being surprised by the content of the stories I read without re-reading the blurbs. This was one of those times. Note to other readers: This book has nothing to do with WWII. Where do I even get these ideas?<br /><br />Instead, 'We Were Liars' tells the story of four young teens. They spend the summer together on Beechwood Island, a private island owned by the Sinclair family. Needless to say, the Sinclair family is filthy rich.<br /><br />The story is centered on Cadence, the oldest granddaughter of Mr. Sinclair. She is her grandfather's favorite. Along with her cousins, she has spent many a summer on her grandfather's island, getting into trouble and taking her privilege for granted.<br /><br />One summer, her Aunt's boyfriend brings along his nephew, Gat. He has lost his own father and his uncle has taken Gat under his wing, so to speak. Despite the obvious differences in race and financial standing, Gat becomes good friends with Cadence and her cousins. Together, they come to be known as "The Four Liars".<br /><br />Cadence and Gat soon become inseparable. He makes her think about life and the wrongs of the world. He brings depth to her pampered existence, prompting thought on topics such as race and social standing. It was young love. It was beautiful.<br /><br />Then, Cadence suffers a terrible accident. She nearly dies, but doctors are able to save her. The accident has left her forever changed though. It has also taken it's toll on her relationships. Worst of all, Gat seems to have abandoned her in her time of need.<br /><br />After a prolonged absence, Cadence returns to the island once again. It is the first of many steps that she will take toward recovery. However, the truth that has alluded her will eventually resurface.<br /><br />I won't say too much because I don't want to spoil this book for anyone. Unlike others, I have to say that I did not predict the big twist at the end. I was completely blindsided. I never saw it coming.<br /><br />Overall, this was a great read for me. At times, it could get a little slow. However, I found myself really enjoying the story of Cadence and the "beautiful Sinclair family". 'We Were Liars' serves as a cautionary tale, warning readers of the consequences of greed, hypocrisy and racism, among others. Things aren't always as "perfect" as they seem when looking in from the outside. This book makes that crystal clear.<br /><br />Check out more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bookaddicthaven.com">www.bookaddicthaven.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9373049168297849585" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

was<br>Expected.</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433196381i/15062688._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="205" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Do you think I lie?..No..They Were..Not me..<br><b>لازم أكتب بلغتي ﻷني مشحون، غاضب وحزين<br>هذه الرواية ألمت قلبي، ولو أنها رواية عادية جدا<br><img
