الألم<br><br>شعرت أنني فهمت الغموض وحللت اللغز<br>وأني شاهدت وقرأت قصصاً كهذه من قبل<br><br>هي عن عائلة ، سينكلير ، عائلة قوية، غنية ، فاشلة ، محطمة<br>هي عن 4 أصدقاء، أقارب، هي عن مرحلة المراهقة، هي عن براءة الأطفال ومرحها<br><br>كانوا 4 كاذبين<br>كانوا 4 لا يريدون شيئا إلا أن يبقوا سويا في جزيرة عائلة سينكلير الخاصة كل صيف كما أعتادوا<br>كانوا 4 أقارب , قريبين جدا في الصيف.. بعيدين جدا بعد ذلك<br>كانوا 4 ، سويا من سن الثامنة حتي الخامسة عشر ....ثم السابعة عشر<br><br>كانوا 4 ، يريدون حياة أفضل ، أنجح، دون أطماع ، دون أحكام مسبقة<br>كاتوا 4 يريدون أن يكونون أكثر طيبة مما يستطيعون ، يريدون ألا يأكلوا أزيد مما يستطيعون هضمه<br><br>كانوا اربعة أقارب وأصدقاء، ولو لفترة الصيف فحسب<br>كانوا أربعة مقربين لبعضهم البعض بحق وليس بزيف كحال عائلاتهم المفككة المتنازعة علي توافه اﻷمور<br><br>كانوا 4 كاذبين<br><br>والمؤلفة تطلب منك في غلاف الرواية الخلفي بأنه إذا سألك أحدهم كيف كانت عائلة سينكلير ، فلتكذب<br><br>فهل سأكذب؟<br>كاﻷربعة<br>الذين كانوا كاذبين<br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433196952i/15062807.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>رواية كهذه ، 225 صفحة فحسب، مكتوبة بلغة تقريرية سهلة جدا ، لا تستحق الحديث عن أحداثها أكثر ، كي تستكشفها بنفسك أفضل، يكفي أن ما أفسدها لي هو تنبؤي الخاص بها<br>شدني لها الأسم الجذاب<br>كــنا كــاذبون<br>فكرة العائلة , النوستاليجا وأيام الصيفية<br><br>ثم شدني الأسلوب السهل , التقريري , الجمل , الذكريات<br>خريطة الجزيرة الخاصة بعائلة سينكلير , القوية , الغنية , الضعيفة , المحطمة<br><br>الجمل البسيطة , لا تتصنع العمق كرواياتنا العربية المتصنعة, الزائفة <br><br>هذه رواية صادقة ....كاذبة<br><br>ولكن<br><br>أنا لم أكذب عندما قلت أن الحبكة عرفتها من بعد ربعها اﻷول <br>وتنبات بنهايتها<br><br>لا أكذب أنني لم أهتم كثيرا بسير اﻷحداث من بعد ربعهااﻷول, وعانيت منها قدر ما كنت أسعي وراء الراويّة -واحدة من اﻷربعة، كادينس، التي تروي الحكاية - لأعرف منها كيف حدث ما توقعته...ما قد نسيته هي نفسها<br>ما عرفته<br>حتي قبل أن تقوله <br>أو تتذكره<br><br>أرهقتني ببراعة بحكايات خيالية عديدة وسط اﻷحداث ، حكايات خيالية غير معروفة<br>فهي تنويعة علي قصص شهيرة معروفة<br>كالملك لير , الجميلة والوحش .. وغيرها من القصص الخيالية<br>كلها تبدأ ب'كان ياما كان <br>كان في ملك عنده 3 بنات<br>كان في ملك عنده 3 أميرات <br> كان في 3 أميرات<br>كان في 3 أخوات<br>كان في 3 وحوش<br>كان في <br>ياما كان<br><br>أسلوبي العجيب في الريفيو هو نفس أسلوب المؤلفة، الراويّة ، الحفيدة الكبري لعائلة سينكلير <br><br>وهي تحكي أيام الصيفية في جزيرتهم الخاصة<br>تحكي<br>أو تكدب<br><br>لا فارق<br>فهم اﻷربعة ، كانوا ، كاذبين<br><br>كل واحد في عائلته البعض لديهم مشاكل ولو 10% من اللي في سينكلير<br>خلافات عائلية للأسف لمستها أحيانا في عائلتي <br>خلافات تفرق العائلات ....خلافات هدامة<br>مين فينا فعلا <br>Sin Clear<br>أكيد مش Sinclair <br><br>وبصراحة , ربما تلك الخلافات الأسرية البسيطة التي قد تكون هادمة هي اكثر ما سبب لي مشاعر قوية تجاه الرواية وجعلني ِأشعر بها أكثر مما توقعت<br><br>دراما عائلية , شبابية , صيفية , معاصرة<br>بلا تكنولوجيا وسيلفي وفيس بوك وانستجرام<br>فقط كتب , لعب الأجازة , ألوان وكراسات تلوين<br>عرائس باربي<br>ليجو<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433200366i/15063441.png" width="400" height="148" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>نوستاليجا جميلة مخلوطة بمرارة , وحادث صعب<br><br>بتستفيد أيه من وجع القلب والحكايات دي<br>ولا حاجة<br><blockquote>“Be a little kinder than you have to.” <br>“Always do what you're afraid to do.” <br>"Never eat anything bigger than your ass."<br>“Do not accept an evil you can change.” </blockquote>
<br>خليك شجاع، أطيب شوية مما تقدر، متاكلش اللي متقدرش تهضمه ، متحكمش علي الناس بعنصرية وأحكام مسبقة<br><br>كلام عادي ، لكن مين قال أن التراجيديا لازم تكون درس باهر ، فصل مهم في رواية، عبرة وعظة .. هذه القصة لا تدعي عمقا مصطنعا<br><br>التراجيديا ، تراجيديا<br>اﻷلم ألم ..... المهم أن تتحمل ، أن تعيش.....ألا تتفرق وتقطع صلاتك العائلية<br><br>تراجيديا، يمكن مش بتوصل رسالة عظيمة ، إلا أن الكلام العادي جدا ده حيحفروا سطورهم بعقلك، قلبك ، روحك<br><blockquote>“Be sad, be sorry-but don't shoulder it.” </blockquote>
<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1433200652ra/15063478.gif" width="400" height="170" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>بكيت، بقدر الخجل اللي بقوله لن يصف شعوري في مكان عام وأنا أحاول السيطرة علي نفسي وأنا أقرأ تلك القصة وتتابعات نهايتها<br><br> عشرون صفحة متعبة بالرغم من النهاية الجميلة <br></b>- The Fault in Our Stars عيد ميلادي 14 يوليو ، مرة أخري من بعد<b><br>تلك النهاية الجميلة<br>الجذابة، الكذابة<br>الكاملة<br>أو النهاية المفتوحة <br><br>لا يهم<br>لكني ظللت أبكي..رغم كل شئ <br>حتي في جزء عادي<br><blockquote>MUMMY BANGS ON my door and calls my name.<br><br> I do not answer.<br><br> An hour later, she bangs again.<br><br> “Let me in, won’t you?”<br><br> “Go away.”<br><br> “Is it a migraine? Just tell me that.”<br><br> “It isn’t a migraine,” I say. “It’s something else.”<br><br> “I love you, Cady,” she says.<br><br> She says it all the time since I got sick, but only now do I see that what Mummy means is,.....</blockquote>
<br>ماذا تعني؟...لا فارق, المهم انها شعرت أن أمها تحبها<br>هذا جعلني أيضا أتأثر كثيرا <br><br>جدا<br><br>ْ~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br>ثلاث نجوم ونصف تقييمي المبدئي , أو 4 ﻷني فقط عرفت الحبكة .... دعوني اناقشها معكم في الجزء المخفي لمن لم يقرأ الرواية بعد<br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[<br>في قصة لإسعاد يونس قدمتها في 1994 ، وجعلتني أبكي جدا ﻷني كنت صغير وقتها وتعاطفت مع البطلة ، الراوية<br>هناك فيلم قوي جدا ومثير وغير متوقع ، وإن كان صديق واحد فقط لي يجزم أنه عرف الحبكة بنصف الفيلم ، هو فيلم<br>The Uninvited (2009)<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433200366i/15063442._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="320" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>شاهد الفيلم بعد الرواية وستفهم قصدي..الفيلم يشبه الرواية بشكل كبير , أو العكس<br><br>وربما إذا كنت من هواة روايات الرعب الجديدة ستجد نفسك تشك في اﻷمر مثلي <br>إذا كنت لم تقرأ الرواية بعد ، أيه اللي جابك هنا؟ <br>عاما أقرأ الرواية لنهايتها .... أنا نفسي كنت متأكد من النهاية ، لكن المغزي والأسلوب هو ما أخترق مشاعري<br>الفكرة ، الهدف<br><br>أربعة كانوا صغارا، علي أعتاب المراهقة<br>أربعة رأوا عائلة يمزقها الجشع، الطمع، خلافات علي توافه اﻷمور<br>أربعة رأوا عائلة تعاني فشل، كسل، إستسهال ، عنصرية<br>أربعة أرادوا التغيير...أرادوا ثورة<br>أربعة كانوا أطفال<br>أربعة كانوا علي أعتاب المراهقة<br><br>أنا نفسي كنت متأكد من النهاية ، لكن  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br>المغزي والأسلوب هو ما أخترق مشاعري<br>هل 4 نجوم كثير، أم أقل <br>هل أنا كاذب<br>هل تركت حكمي لمشاعري؟ هل كما طلبت المؤلفة بالبداية كذبت؟<br>هم كانوا كاذبون<br><br><br>ما رأيك أنت؟<br>A Must Read<br><br></b><br>محمد العربي <br>من 30 مايو 2015<br>إلي 1 يونيو 2015<br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_988178827" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/988178827" />
    <a title="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2744708-jess-the-shelf-declared-bibliophile"><img alt="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1606058182p2/2744708.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/988178827?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile" href="/user/show/2744708-jess-the-shelf-declared-bibliophile">Jess the Shelf-Declared Bibliophile</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer988178827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6027660064801341209">OH MY GOD. Hands down, this is by far the most amazing book I've read so far this year, and possibly a good part of last year. I went into it knowing hardly anything about it, which is the way it should be. Now that I'm done, I literally want to pick it up and start it all over again.<br/><br/>I know alot of people dislike the disjointed writing, but it didn't bother me in the least. I flew through this book today despite being extremely busy at work, and I came home and immediately picked it back up. I j</span>
  <span id="freeText6027660064801341209" style="display:none">OH MY GOD. Hands down, this is by far the most amazing book I've read so far this year, and possibly a good part of last year. I went into it knowing hardly anything about it, which is the way it should be. Now that I'm done, I literally want to pick it up and start it all over again.<br><br>I know alot of people dislike the disjointed writing, but it didn't bother me in the least. I flew through this book today despite being extremely busy at work, and I came home and immediately picked it back up. I just finished it after taking far too long of a bath and becoming raisin-y just because I couldn't bear to put the book down. I finished and got out of the bath (which had doubled in water volume due to tears) and IMMEDIATELY came to write my review. Still a little weepy. <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/girl%20sobbing" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380405908ra/791330.gif" alt="girl sobbing photo: sobbing sobbing_zps29276070.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But seriously, GO READ THIS. Stop what you're doing and go get it RIGHT NOW. It will blow you away. <br><br>As for me? I'm gonna go eat a bowl of Cocoa Pebbles and find something happy to read. I'll be ok, really.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/sobbing" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398829924ra/9469586.gif" alt="sobbing photo: SOBBING tumblr_m0hmrgSLXk1qhejhu.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6027660064801341209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_812548747" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/812548747" />
    <a title="Mary Christensen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17419283-mary-christensen"><img alt="Mary Christensen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1389088232p2/17419283.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/812548747?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Christensen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Christensen" href="/user/show/17419283-mary-christensen">Mary Christensen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer812548747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13855664846273039310">A really unfortunate novel by the author of the much better <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1629601.The_Disreputable_History_of_Frankie_Landau_Banks' title='The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks by E. Lockhart' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks</a>. A completely unconvincing twist in the last twenty pages resolves the mystery in a way that is both improbably gruesome and also lightly dismissed by the author. <br/><br/>The real moral questions raised by the subject of the book, including racism, land ownership, inheritance, materialism, greed, and manipulation, are acted out in flat, white-hat/black-hat morality plays by stock characters of li</span>
  <span id="freeText13855664846273039310" style="display:none">A really unfortunate novel by the author of the much better <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1629601.The_Disreputable_History_of_Frankie_Landau_Banks" title="The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks by E. Lockhart" rel="nofollow noopener">The Disreputable History of Frankie Landau-Banks</a>. A completely unconvincing twist in the last twenty pages resolves the mystery in a way that is both improbably gruesome and also lightly dismissed by the author. <br /><br />The real moral questions raised by the subject of the book, including racism, land ownership, inheritance, materialism, greed, and manipulation, are acted out in flat, white-hat/black-hat morality plays by stock characters of little or no complexity. Those questions are then answered by an intruding author's voice that patronizes the reader by declaring single answers to every moral issue raised. The same problems exist on the literary level. Interesting tools, like allegory and literary allusions, are brought into the narrative, but are then executed in a heavy-handed, amateurish way that leaves no room for the reader to respond or engage, simply enter stage right, spell out their own significance, and exit stage left. Finally, the main character, despite being the pov character in a novel of psychological recovery, is a completely empty vehicle for plot and the author's voice, with no identifiable personality or characteristics by the end of the book. <br /><br />The politics in the book are good. The plot is an unfortunate mismatch of borrowed material. The characters are overused stereotypes. The incorporation of sophisticated literary techniques is clumsy and embarrassing. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13855664846273039310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13440674751864957040"><i> “Tragedy is ugly and tangled, stupid and confusing.” </i><br/><br/>Everyone warned me about the twist in this book! I did well not to get spoiled, as it was definitely a shock horror moment. <br/><br/>A patriarch, his three daughters and their children summer every year on Beechwood Island, where each of the three daughters had a house for themselves and their children. <br/>They are all rich, well off and ignorant. The three oldest grandchildren and their family friend are the closest. They refer to themselves as the ‘Lia</span>
  <span id="freeText13440674751864957040" style="display:none"><i> “Tragedy is ugly and tangled, stupid and confusing.” </i><br /><br />Everyone warned me about the twist in this book! I did well not to get spoiled, as it was definitely a shock horror moment. <br /><br />A patriarch, his three daughters and their children summer every year on Beechwood Island, where each of the three daughters had a house for themselves and their children. <br />They are all rich, well off and ignorant. The three oldest grandchildren and their family friend are the closest. They refer to themselves as the ‘Liars’. Johnny, Mirren, Gat and Cadence. <br /><br />The summer of their fifteenth year, Cady has an accident. Hits her head, and suffers severe migraines that can knock her out for days at a time. She misses the entirety of summer sixteen - while on holiday with her dad in Europe. <br /><br />When she returns for Summer Seventeen, things don’t feel the same. The adults are quiet, drinking too much and generally being secretive. <br /><br />Her migraines and head injury cause Cady to suffer memory blanks from summer fifteen. It doesn’t help that her ‘Liars’ won’t fill her in on anything, having been told it’s best if she tries to remember things on her own. <br /><br />What eventually comes to light regarding the events of summer fifteen will absolutely blow your mind! Though I knew there would be a shock twist, I was in no way prepared for the one they gave me! <br /><br />A relatively short book, I blitzed through it, and highly recommend. <br /><br />***************************<br /><br />Well fuck<br /><br />RTC</span>

<div id="review_791732342" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/791732342" />
    <a title="Giselle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle"><img alt="Giselle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1310159877p2/4800103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/791732342?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Giselle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Giselle" href="/user/show/4800103-giselle">Giselle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4800103-giselle?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer791732342" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8281435520520086178"><i>We Were Liars</i> is an incredible, heartbreaking read that really messes with your mind until the very end. The writing, while not for everyone I'm sure, had me mesmerized. It's so different and poetic and full of carefully crafted imagery. It's a writing style that's really out of the box, you'll either love it or hate it. Me, I was thoroughly compelled. <br/><br/>The plot itself is one you can't talk about or read about as you're bound to find out spoilers. It's the kind of story where the story itself is </span>
  <span id="freeText8281435520520086178" style="display:none"><i>We Were Liars</i> is an incredible, heartbreaking read that really messes with your mind until the very end. The writing, while not for everyone I'm sure, had me mesmerized. It's so different and poetic and full of carefully crafted imagery. It's a writing style that's really out of the box, you'll either love it or hate it. Me, I was thoroughly compelled. <br><br>The plot itself is one you can't talk about or read about as you're bound to find out spoilers. It's the kind of story where the story itself is a spoiler from very early on. There are hints floating in every corner, pieces of this carefully constructed puzzle laid out for you to put together. My advice: go into this with zero expectations and you might find yourself as enthralled as I was! Although it's a twist I have seen before in different variations (and thus I wasn't completely caught off guard by the ending), it never fails to give me goosebumps and sting at my poor heart. <br><br>The cast is large, and the dark, twisted fairy-tale-like quality is ever-present inside this tale revolving around greed, power, and material things. This tone is maintained with actual short fairy-tale retellings scattered throughout that bore an eerie resemblance to the present story. It did take me a bit to get all the characters and different disaccords in order - the cryptic, mind-boggly nature of this plot and writing makes it hard to make sense of what's being conveyed at times, but this is clearly purposeful and I ended up impressed by its cleverness. <br><br>But anyways, this review has to stay short because, la la la - no spoilers - it's <i>that</i> kind of read. Plus the blurb told me to lie, so maybe this review is full of crock and this book is just a bunch of dancing elephants. In any case - 4 stars all the way!<br><br>--<br><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for review.</i><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit my blog at <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Xpresso Reads</a> <a href="http://www.xpressoreads.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388702323i/7905232.png" width="380" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8281435520520086178" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2501433502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12947500002746857839"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1565289127i/27957672._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote> Be normal.<br/>Because you are.<br/>Because you can be</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/>I am so, so glad I decided to pick this up. It was amazing. I am going to do my best to review this without spoilers. Here it goes. The beginning is not very interesting. Unfortunately, I've seen this fact drive away a ton of readers. This is why I suggest the audio. Just keep listening, it ends amazingly. It definitely took me a while to get used the storytelling style that is so unique to E. Lockhart. The ending was amazing. It was like </span>
  <span id="freeText12947500002746857839" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1565289127i/27957672._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote> Be normal.<br>Because you are.<br>Because you can be</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>I am so, so glad I decided to pick this up. It was amazing. I am going to do my best to review this without spoilers. Here it goes. The beginning is not very interesting. Unfortunately, I've seen this fact drive away a ton of readers. This is why I suggest the audio. Just keep listening, it ends amazingly. It definitely took me a while to get used the storytelling style that is so unique to E. Lockhart. The ending was amazing. It was like nothing I was imagining. I can't even give vague hints though without ruining the entire story. Aside from the mystery, I really enjoyed the family aspect of this book evening they were the definition of "dysfunctional".<br><br>Bottom Line:<br>5 Solid Stars: A great story with a plot twist like no other.<br>Age Recommendation: 13+<br>TW: Injuries, Substance Abuse<br><br>| <a href="https://Goodreads.com/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://tuckerthereader.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://Pinterest.com/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a> | <a href="https://linkedin.com/in/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">LinkedIn</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC1JLAbHwaeQ5YwayF3UhjWw" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="https://instagram.com/tuckeralmengor" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_795519220" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/795519220" />
    <a title="Emily Crowe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3873198-emily-crowe"><img alt="Emily Crowe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1276538029p2/3873198.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/795519220?book_show_action=true">Dec 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily Crowe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily Crowe" href="/user/show/3873198-emily-crowe">Emily Crowe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385741262" href="/book/show/18339662-we-were-liars">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3873198-emily-crowe?shelf=ya-or-middle-reader">ya-or-middle-reader</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3873198-emily-crowe?shelf=2013">2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer795519220" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4983507053456918133">Eh. This was not the book for me, which I was disappointed to discover after two book-friends and an admired blogger all raved about this one. If I had expected less, I probably would have enjoyed it more, but as it stands, it ticked a few boxes for my various readerly pet peeves:<br/><br/>1) A first person narrator<br/>2) An unreliable narrator (This is not a spoiler. Read the title. And the narrator has amnesia.)<br/>3) The narrator has amnesia.<br/>4) In the last 30 pages or so, the narrator/author make a big reveal </span>
  <span id="freeText4983507053456918133" style="display:none">Eh. This was not the book for me, which I was disappointed to discover after two book-friends and an admired blogger all raved about this one. If I had expected less, I probably would have enjoyed it more, but as it stands, it ticked a few boxes for my various readerly pet peeves:<br /><br />1) A first person narrator<br />2) An unreliable narrator (This is not a spoiler. Read the title. And the narrator has amnesia.)<br />3) The narrator has amnesia.<br />4) In the last 30 pages or so, the narrator/author make a big reveal that negates several "facts" that the reader has necessarily taken at face value for the previous 180 pages. <br /><br />If those things don't bother you, or at least don't bother you as much as they bother me, then you'll probably enjoy this book. I would have liked it more if it weren't hyped the way it was. I've seen the same tropes done better, and from what I knew of this author, I frankly expected more. <br /><br />Beyond that, I thought that the sibling and cousin relationships were particularly ill-drawn and I had trouble suspending my disbelief that these kids spend every summer together on their own private island, year after year, and yet have weirdly stilted dialogue. The adult relationships and the parent-child relationships all rang true to me, though. <br /><br />The big reveal at the end is incredibly tragic but only somewhat of a stunner, but unlike the folks here who claimed to have cried buckets, I was dry-eyed. If you read enough fiction featuring amnesiac and/or mentally unbalanced main characters, the ending to this book won't come totally out of left field. The only thing that left me truly feeling WTF was the actual execution of the Liars's Big Plan That Backfired. It's almost like they don't know the basics of physics/chemistry/accelerants. I won't say more because beyond there, spoilers lie. </span>
  <a data-text-id="4983507053456918133" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TGW0yOxiu6ozcEIrTXGg4q01auYaCmXwQSCeL8qFNUn8xSlB/vO8mXJu+TUMmUcryY1lIKaUyrlZjEPpTy0tsw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RJwSnYd4VBmiuIQBRz/4A36wPcNG8nQiCzIGk81SX1n0PI8UlelTKuOmPx8G1x/KGggyBfps22sTnttVSPpHow==')})
  }
